**GT:** `7.723*epsilon**3 + 36.659*epsilon**0.2144*exp(-82.437/(8.314*T)) + epsilon*1.336*(T - 327.264)**2`

Let me expand the last term:
`epsilon*1.336*(T - 327.264)**2 = epsilon*1.336*(T² - 654.529*T + 107,102.0) = 1.336*epsilon*T² - 874.85*epsilon*T + 143,088.3*epsilon`

So GT = `7.723*epsilon**3 + 36.659*epsilon**0.2144*exp(-9.916/T) + 1.336*epsilon*T² - 874.85*epsilon*T + 143,088.3*epsilon`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `epsilon**3` (polynomial in epsilon)
2. `epsilon**0.2144 * exp(-c/T)` (fractional power times Arrhenius-type exponential)
3. `epsilon * T²` (cross term)
4. `epsilon * T` (cross term)
5. `epsilon` (linear in epsilon)

The key challenge is the `exp(-c/T)` term. This is NOT equivalent to `exp(c*T)`, `log(T)`, `T**n`, or any polynomial/simple function of T.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `exp(-c/T)` or equivalent:

Most candidates use `exp(T*c)`, `log(T*c + 1)`, `T**c`, `cos(T*c)`, `sin(T*c)`, polynomial in T, or `(T+c)**c` forms. None of these can match `exp(-c/T)`.

Let me carefully check which candidates could potentially match:

**Candidate 9:** `T*c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*epsilon*(T + c7)**c8`

The term `T*epsilon**c1` is linear in T. So we can't get the exponential term.
